    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="review_119810895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119810895" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119810895?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177891-kat-hooper?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119810895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13175971829884571183">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>.<br/><br/>I read The Farseer Saga years ago and have since considered it one of my favorite fantasy epics. It's one (along with The Lord of the Rings and Memory, Sorrow and Thorn) that I often suggest to new fantasy readers. But after more than a decade of reading deeper and further into fantasy literature, I've often wondered how well this saga would now appeal to my more mature (I hope) palate. When Tantor Audio recently released The Farseer Saga on audio, I was o</span>
  <span id="freeText13175971829884571183" style="display:none">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>.<br /><br />I read The Farseer Saga years ago and have since considered it one of my favorite fantasy epics. It's one (along with The Lord of the Rings and Memory, Sorrow and Thorn) that I often suggest to new fantasy readers. But after more than a decade of reading deeper and further into fantasy literature, I've often wondered how well this saga would now appeal to my more mature (I hope) palate. When Tantor Audio recently released The Farseer Saga on audio, I was overjoyed and considered this to be my sign that it's time to re-visit the six duchies.<br /><br />When Assassin's Apprentice arrived in the mail, I yanked out the CD that was currently in my computer, tossed it aside (sorry, Ray Bradbury) and stuck in the first Assassin's Apprentice disc. My lips trembled as I mouthed the name of the narrator: Paul Boehmer… Never heard of him. Is he good enough to portray Fitz, one of my all-time favorite fantasy characters? And… my stomach twisted… will Fitz be the same boy I came to care so much for so many years ago?<br /><br />Within minutes I was reabsorbed into the world of FitzChivalry Farseer, that insecure, lonely boy who has so much potential but, due to his illegitimate birth and his peculiar abilities with animals, never gets what he deserves. Fitz was just as I remembered and Paul Boehmer portrayed him (and all the other characters) beautifully. (Except that at one point he incorrectly used the word “prisoner” instead of “poisoner.”)<br /><br />Robin Hobb's prose was as nice as I remembered, too — straightforward and simple. It never calls attention to itself (and therefore away from the story). Her characters are engaging and nicely portrayed, though a couple of her villains are overdone. Her animal characters are especially notable and, though I'm not a dog lover, I can't help but be emotionally connected to Fitz's canine companions. My second read also gave me a greater appreciation for Hobb's world-building as I encountered tidbits of information that are relevant to her later works (Tawny Man, Liveship Traders, Rain Wilds).<br /><br />My only disappointment is that I don't have the next book, Royal Assassin, in my hands yet. I'm not sure why I'm so eager to torture myself again with this story because I know what's going to happen. Things don't always go well for Fitz. His story is heart-wrenching, and I know I'll be emotionally drained after I finish it. But I'm going to love every minute of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13175971829884571183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer740952783984537182">It was a very enjoyable book, and I think my favorite thing about it was reading a well-written book in from the first-person perspective. I think Robin Hobb was masterful in that aspect of the writing. It adds a fun dynamic to a story when you can get completely get inside the head of a character. One impressive thing that was done with the first person view was how little we know... because the character doesn't know them. For example: There's all sorts of court intrigue and secret plots going</span>
  <span id="freeText740952783984537182" style="display:none">It was a very enjoyable book, and I think my favorite thing about it was reading a well-written book in from the first-person perspective. I think Robin Hobb was masterful in that aspect of the writing. It adds a fun dynamic to a story when you can get completely get inside the head of a character. One impressive thing that was done with the first person view was how little we know... because the character doesn't know them. For example: There's all sorts of court intrigue and secret plots going on in the story that you only get small glimpses of, yet they obviously steer the course of the plot significantly. Little explanation is given to these, simply because the main character is a young boy who doesn't know the particulars himself. I enjoyed reading it, and am happily continuing on with the 3-book series.</span>

  <span id="freeText11099495652712505145" style="display:none">Summer reading book reviews, book #12, "Assassin's Apprentice" by Robin Hobb.... This is the first book in a trilogy. I found it a nicely written, intelligent fantasy with a compelling and sympathetic protagonist: a young boy who has a very tough childhood, growing up as the bastard son of a prince. I did wish, however, that the central character would suffer a little less, or at least be less isolated in his suffering. <div id="review_2260015549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2260015549" />
    <a title="Deb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48641197-deb"><img alt="Deb" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2260015549?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deb" href="/user/show/48641197-deb">Deb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2260015549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13964481208382444081">I really liked this book, but found it so much harder to get into than other Robin Hobb books that I've read. After three failed attempts, I finally persevered and read it all. It was a good read, and left me wanting more. <br/>It may be good marketing practice to follow the end of a book with the next few chapters of the next but it winds me up no end. It led me to believe that there were another few chapters of story to go, so it seemed to end too suddenly, with a hasty round up of loose ends. I li</span>
  <span id="freeText13964481208382444081" style="display:none">I really liked this book, but found it so much harder to get into than other Robin Hobb books that I've read. After three failed attempts, I finally persevered and read it all. It was a good read, and left me wanting more. <br />It may be good marketing practice to follow the end of a book with the next few chapters of the next but it winds me up no end. It led me to believe that there were another few chapters of story to go, so it seemed to end too suddenly, with a hasty round up of loose ends. I like to savour a good ending, and felt a bit cheated.<br />Still going to try the next one in the series though :-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13964481208382444081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3465745556" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3465745556" />
    <a title="Gary Currier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/96574956-gary-currier"><img alt="Gary Currier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556414427p2/96574956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3465745556?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary Currier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary Currier" href="/user/show/96574956-gary-currier">Gary Currier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3465745556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6384899857747116012">The book was compelling and it made me actually rush through it in a desperate need to see what happens. The build is slow along with the main character Fitz. I have a pet peeve that a character that is supposed to be quick witted at least figure out somethings along the way. Fitz never does until after the damage is done. By sure luck he survives, at the loss of others he seems to want to help. Other than that this book was a completely awesome read. Thank you Robin Hobb, for a great read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1236027313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1236027313" />
    <a title="Radhikarani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8267672-radhikarani"><img alt="Radhikarani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477204970p2/8267672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1236027313?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Radhikarani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Radhikarani" href="/user/show/8267672-radhikarani">Radhikarani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1236027313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17369863597419044084">A friend who isn't much of a reader recommended this series to me since I love fantasy fiction. This is a fantasy fiction set with medieval customs in a fictional land with a bastard son of the king to be and is his story as much as the story of the kingdom.<br/><br/>It's easy to like Fitz - you meet him when he's a kid and see him grow in the shadows and cared for by both his royal relatives and the people who bring him up. <br/><br/>If you have read Wheel of Time, this is a watered down version of the supernatura</span>
  <span id="freeText17369863597419044084" style="display:none">A friend who isn't much of a reader recommended this series to me since I love fantasy fiction. This is a fantasy fiction set with medieval customs in a fictional land with a bastard son of the king to be and is his story as much as the story of the kingdom.<br /><br />It's easy to like Fitz - you meet him when he's a kid and see him grow in the shadows and cared for by both his royal relatives and the people who bring him up. <br /><br />If you have read Wheel of Time, this is a watered down version of the supernatural powers mentioned and the quest to master these powers / skills. <br /><br />*spoiler alert<br /><br />The first book was alright. there is however one scene from the book that is very Potterish - when the love of a young puppy brings Fitz back from a dark suicidal mood. It is my favorite scene of Book 1. Much like how Nighteyes saves Fitz in Book 2 with "we are pack" in a battle of skill and wills.<br /><br />Honestly after book 1, I wasn't sure if I was interested enough to read book 2. But my friend edged me on. And I will admit I liked Book 2 better than Book 1. It sucked me in and I felt like Rip Van Winkle sleeping in one age and waking up in another juggling email and traffic lights with Fitz's love story and the politics of the six duchies.<br /><br />Would I recommend the book? Yes. Its a good read,not as complicated as the Wheel of Time or Lord of the Rings. Nor does UT have too many characters or places to confuse a reader.<br /><br />3/5 for this decent but average fantasy fiction book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17369863597419044084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_485965714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485965714" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11352701-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343688051p2/11352701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/485965714?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/11352701-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer485965714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8105548610795859628">This novel was everything I wanted, even though I had read a few reviews that claimed it lacked focus and action. Hobb reintroduces us to FitzChivalry Farseer, the royal assassin of the Farseer line, and all of his friends and enemies. The mysterious Redship raiders are back, plundering the coastline while the King of the Six Duchies slowly descends into senility. Fitz feels helpless to stop his beloved lord's decline, but works hand in glove with the King's son, Verity, to discover the truth be</span>
  <span id="freeText8105548610795859628" style="display:none">This novel was everything I wanted, even though I had read a few reviews that claimed it lacked focus and action. Hobb reintroduces us to FitzChivalry Farseer, the royal assassin of the Farseer line, and all of his friends and enemies. The mysterious Redship raiders are back, plundering the coastline while the King of the Six Duchies slowly descends into senility. Fitz feels helpless to stop his beloved lord's decline, but works hand in glove with the King's son, Verity, to discover the truth behind all of the disasters plaguing the kingdom. <br /><br />Like the first book in this series, the plot doesn't seem to move too fast until you hit the last 100 pages or so and realize that Hobb has been slowly building up to a stunning climax. She keeps measuring plot and characterization out in equal detail. As you begin, just recognize that she has lit a slow fuse, but the explosion at the end of the novel is such that it makes all the early reading worth it.<br /><br />I am so excited to see where the last book goes! Picked it up today and am going to dive in tonight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8105548610795859628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17268583446667960958">I've enjoyed Robin Hobb's writing so far. She writes full-bodied characters, includes just the right amount of description and has been able to weave an appealing plot that aroused my curiosity enough to keep me turning the pages. Although I can't say this was a gripping story, it was enjoyable enough that I started reading the second book, which I'm half way through right now but I feel like we are just going through the same motions as in book one: <i>he visits this person, he visits that person,</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17268583446667960958" style="display:none">I've enjoyed Robin Hobb's writing so far. She writes full-bodied characters, includes just the right amount of description and has been able to weave an appealing plot that aroused my curiosity enough to keep me turning the pages. Although I can't say this was a gripping story, it was enjoyable enough that I started reading the second book, which I'm half way through right now but I feel like we are just going through the same motions as in book one: <i>he visits this person, he visits that person, he has some personal struggles which he is striving to overcome and he's doing some things he's been told not to...and there's a bit of this going on over there which may or may not threaten him and the people around him, etc. </i>. So I'm sorry to say I've set book two aside for now but I'd like to finish this series so one day I'm sure I will get back to it.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140044831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9210091658742750558">Assassin's Apprentice is one of the best books I've ever read, filled with characters that feel very real and human.<br/><br/>In a fantasy genre flooded with unoriginal plots, sub-par characterization, and terrible writing, the Farseer series literally stands out as almost flawless. Whether the story appeals to you or not is entirely up to your personal preferences, but these books are still excellent in the sense that the plot contains a fresh and original twist on several fantasy elements, the character</span>
  <span id="freeText9210091658742750558" style="display:none">Assassin's Apprentice is one of the best books I've ever read, filled with characters that feel very real and human.<br /><br />In a fantasy genre flooded with unoriginal plots, sub-par characterization, and terrible writing, the Farseer series literally stands out as almost flawless. Whether the story appeals to you or not is entirely up to your personal preferences, but these books are still excellent in the sense that the plot contains a fresh and original twist on several fantasy elements, the characterizations of everyone in the books are consistent, realistic, and well-fleshed out, and the writing style is smooth and elegant.</span>

  <span id="freeText10947910016799897162" style="display:none">Loved it. I'm amazed at the difference between this series, and the Rainwilds series. The Rain Wild series doesn't seem to have the same depth of character, although, I've read enough now to know they're related, so perhaps reading this series will give some insight into that one.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249541220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14062942737722913807">This book was wonderfully written. I love that it reads like a memoir, and I love the realness of the characters (for better or worse). Fitz was difficult for me to handle at times, he just couldn't seem to get his head in the game this book, and as a result his country and his loved ones suffered. Because of this, I had to keep setting the book down and taking a break. I just kept getting too angry at Regal and frustrated at Fitz! It really was a wonderful read, though, and I really look forwar</span>
  <span id="freeText14062942737722913807" style="display:none">This book was wonderfully written. I love that it reads like a memoir, and I love the realness of the characters (for better or worse). Fitz was difficult for me to handle at times, he just couldn't seem to get his head in the game this book, and as a result his country and his loved ones suffered. Because of this, I had to keep setting the book down and taking a break. I just kept getting too angry at Regal and frustrated at Fitz! It really was a wonderful read, though, and I really look forward to the 3rd book! I highly suggest this trilogy!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E50CbfvRQCx7OhJhn01UdNeBy7Gr/y2ihQ3rIE+YLLPzuCGYa+5kOY2FHOBrll546Ag8y0yvAjbwgC5RLyxcMg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6591663288926774022">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText6591663288926774022" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>
